{
  "content": "# Istio Pilot Discovery Service: Architecture Document\n\n## Overview\n\nIstio Pilot's Discovery Service is the subsystem inside `istiod` that translates Istio's high-level mesh configuration into Envoy-specific xDS resources and streams those resources to every connected sidecar, gateway, and ztunnel proxy. The subsystem is built around four tightly coupled layers:\n\n1. **`DiscoveryServer`** \u2014 the gRPC server that owns proxy connections and orchestrates pushes\n2. **The ADS/Delta Connection Model** \u2014 the per-proxy streaming logic and push pipeline\n3. **`PushContext`** \u2014 the immutable configuration snapshot computed before each fleet-wide push\n4. **Service Registry** \u2014 the data source that tracks live services and endpoints\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer \u2014 The xDS gRPC Server\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`\n\n### What It Owns\n\n`DiscoveryServer` is the central coordinator. It implements the Envoy `AggregatedDiscoveryService` gRPC service and sits at the boundary between Istio's internal data model and Envoy's wire protocol. Its fields define every aspect of the push lifecycle:\n\n| Field | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `adsClients map[string]*Connection` | Registry of every live proxy connection, keyed by connection ID |\n| `pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest` | Inbound buffer for raw update events before debouncing |\n| `pushQueue *PushQueue` | Ordered queue of (connection, pushRequest) pairs after debouncing |\n| `concurrentPushLimit chan struct{}` | Semaphore limiting how many proxy pushes run in parallel (`features.PushThrottle`) |\n| `RequestRateLimit *rate.Limiter` | Token-bucket rate limiter applied to new connection requests |\n| `Cache model.XdsCache` | Shared LRU cache of already-generated xDS resources |\n| `Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator` | Plugin map from typeURL (or proxy type + typeURL) to the code that builds that resource |\n| `InboundUpdates / CommittedUpdates *atomic.Int64` | Lag counters for monitoring how many config events are queued vs. processed |\n| `DebounceOptions` | Configurable `DebounceAfter` / `debounceMax` windows |\n\n### Initialization and Readiness\n\n`NewDiscoveryServer` (`discovery.go:141`) constructs the struct. The server does **not** accept connections until `CachesSynced()` is called (`discovery.go:205`), which sets `serverReady = true`. This prevents Envoy proxies from connecting while Kubernetes informer caches are still warming up \u2014 a guard against a class of \"empty config\" reconnection storms documented in [#25495](https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/25495).\n\n`Start()` (`discovery.go:214`) launches four goroutines:\n- `handleUpdates` \u2014 reads from `pushChannel` and debounces events\n- `periodicRefreshMetrics` \u2014 updates Prometheus gauges every 10s from the current `PushContext`\n- `sendPushes` \u2014 drains `pushQueue` and sends events to individual proxy goroutines\n- `Cache.Run` \u2014 background LRU eviction loop\n\n### Debouncing\n\nAll changes \u2014 whether from Kubernetes watchers, Istio CRDs, or service registry events \u2014 enter the system via `ConfigUpdate(req *model.PushRequest)` (`discovery.go:299`), which appends to `pushChannel`. The `debounce()` function (`discovery.go:331`) acts as a sliding-window accumulator:\n\n1. On receiving an event, it records `lastConfigUpdateTime` and starts a `DebounceAfter` timer.\n2. If another event arrives within that window, requests are **merged** (via `PushRequest.Merge()`) and the timer resets.\n3. Once the system is quiet for `DebounceAfter` time, or the total wait has exceeded `debounceMax`, the merged `PushRequest` is forwarded to `Push()`.\n4. EDS (endpoint-only) updates bypass debouncing entirely when `enableEDSDebounce = false`, so pod scale-ups propagate immediately.\n\nThis design means that a burst of 50 simultaneous CRD changes results in a single full push, not 50 separate pushes.\n\n### Push Coordination: CDS \u2192 EDS \u2192 LDS \u2192 RDS Push Order\n\nThe `PushOrder` slice (`ads.go:499`) defines the strict ordering in which xDS types are pushed to each proxy:\n\n```\nCDS \u2192 EDS \u2192 LDS \u2192 RDS \u2192 SDS \u2192 Address \u2192 Workload \u2192 WorkloadAuthorization\n```\n\nThis order matters because Envoy requires clusters to exist before routes can reference them. Any type not in `PushOrder` is pushed after the known types in undefined order.\n\n### Concurrent Push Throttling\n\n`doSendPushes` (`discovery.go:457`) implements a producer loop: it acquires `concurrentPushLimit` (a buffered channel used as a semaphore) before calling `queue.Dequeue()`. The `doneFunc` released at completion reads back from the semaphore. This ensures at most `features.PushThrottle` proxies receive config simultaneously, preventing CPU saturation during large fleet-wide pushes.\n\n### Cache Management\n\n`dropCacheForRequest` (`discovery.go:247`) is called both before and after `initPushContext`. For `Forced` pushes (JWT key rotation, config deleted) it calls `Cache.ClearAll()`; for targeted updates it calls `Cache.Clear(req.ConfigsUpdated)` which evicts only the cache entries that depend on the changed configs (via the `configIndex` map in `pilot/pkg/model/typed_xds_cache.go`).\n\nThe `typedXdsCache` (`pilot/pkg/model/typed_xds_cache.go`) is an LRU keyed by a generator-specific cache key. Each entry records which `ConfigKey` values it depends on. `Clear(configs)` efficiently looks up only the affected entries instead of flushing the whole cache, which is critical for EDS-only incremental updates.\n\n### Shutdown\n\n`Shutdown()` (`discovery.go:525`) calls `closeJwksResolver()` and `pushQueue.ShutDown()`. The `ShutDown` call broadcasts to all goroutines blocked on `Dequeue`, causing them to exit cleanly.\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`, `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go`\n\n### Establishing a Stream\n\n`StreamAggregatedResources` (`ads.go:183`) is the gRPC entry point for the state-of-the-world xDS protocol. It delegates immediately to `Stream()`, which:\n\n1. Rejects the connection if the server is not ready or the rate limiter is exhausted.\n2. Authenticates the caller via `s.authenticate(ctx)`, which runs all registered `Authenticators` (mTLS certificate validators or JWT verifiers) and returns a list of SPIFFE identity strings.\n3. Ensures a `PushContext` exists (`globalPushContext().InitContext(...)`).\n4. Creates a `Connection` via `newConnection()` and hands it to `xds.Stream(con)` (the shared transport-layer loop in `pkg/xds`).\n\n`DeltaAggregatedResources` (`ads.go:466`) mirrors this flow for the incremental xDS (delta) protocol, delegating to `StreamDeltas()` in `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go`.\n\n### The Connection Type\n\n```go\ntype Connection struct {\n    xds.Connection          // transport state: stream, push channel, stop channel\n    node        *core.Node  // raw Envoy node proto\n    proxy       *model.Proxy // fully-initialized Istio proxy model\n    deltaStream DeltaDiscoveryStream\n    deltaReqChan chan *discovery.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\n    s   *DiscoveryServer\n    ids []string            // authenticated SPIFFE identities\n}\n```\n\n`xds.Connection` (from `pkg/xds`) owns the bidirectional gRPC stream, a per-proxy `pushChannel` for incoming `Event` objects, and an `InitializedCh` semaphore that gates pushes until the proxy is fully initialized.\n\n### Proxy Initialization\n\n`initConnection` (`ads.go:239`) runs on the first request:\n\n1. `initProxyMetadata` \u2014 parses the Envoy `Node.Metadata` proto into a `model.Proxy` struct, setting `ClusterID`, `Type` (SidecarProxy, Router, Ztunnel, Waypoint), and other fields.\n2. `addCon` \u2014 registers the connection in `adsClients` **before** full initialization. This is intentional: if a new `PushContext` is created between `addCon` and `initializeProxy`, the proxy will still receive the new push rather than getting a stale snapshot.\n3. `MarkInitialized()` \u2014 opens `InitializedCh`, unblocking the push sender.\n4. `initializeProxy` \u2014 calls `computeProxyState` which sets `ServiceTargets` (services this pod is an endpoint of), computes `SidecarScope`, and assigns the correct `XdsResourceGenerator` based on `proxy.Metadata.Generator`.\n\n### Request Processing\n\n`processRequest` (`ads.go:138`) handles each incoming `DiscoveryRequest` from Envoy:\n\n- Health check pings (typeURL `HealthInfoType`) are routed to the workload health check handler.\n- Debug URLs (prefix `istio.io/debug`) trigger an immediate response bypassing normal watch state.\n- All other requests go through `xds.ShouldRespond()` which checks nonce, ACK/NACK state, and subscription changes. If the proxy is simply ACKing, the function returns `shouldRespond = false` and no work is done.\n- For new subscriptions or explicit requests, a `PushRequest{Full: true, Reason: ProxyRequest}` is built and passed to `pushXds`.\n\n### Push to a Single Proxy\n\n`pushConnection` (`ads.go:471`) is called by the push goroutine for each proxy when its turn comes out of `PushQueue`:\n\n1. For full pushes, re-runs `computeProxyState` to update the proxy's service targets, labels, and SidecarScope against the current `PushContext`.\n2. Calls `ProxyNeedsPush(proxy, req)` \u2014 `DefaultProxyNeedsPush` calls `filterRelevantUpdates` (`proxy_dependencies.go:36`) which filters `ConfigsUpdated` to only configs the proxy actually depends on. If the result is empty, the push is skipped entirely.\n3. Iterates over `watchedResourcesByOrder()` \u2014 the proxy's active resource subscriptions sorted by `PushOrder` \u2014 and calls `pushXds` for each.\n\n`pushXds` (`xdsgen.go:101`) is the final step: it calls `gen.Generate(proxy, watchedResource, req)` and, if resources are returned, wraps them in a `DiscoveryResponse` proto and sends via the gRPC stream.\n\n### Fleet-Wide Broadcast: StartPush\n\n`AdsPushAll` \u2192 `StartPush` (`ads.go:561,581`) implements the fan-out: it iterates over every connection returned by `AllClients()` and calls `pushQueue.Enqueue(con, req)`. The `PushQueue` (`pilot/pkg/xds/pushqueue.go`) coalesces: if a connection already has a pending push, the new request is merged with `CopyMerge`, preserving the oldest start time and OR-ing the `Full` flag. This prevents a proxy from queuing hundreds of individual EDS updates during a rapid endpoint churn.\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext \u2014 Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`\n\n### What PushContext Holds\n\n`PushContext` is an **immutable snapshot** of all configuration relevant to generating xDS. It is created once per push cycle and then shared (read-only) across every concurrent generator call. Its major indexes are:\n\n| Index | Contents |\n|---|---|\n| `ServiceIndex` | All services by namespace visibility (`private`, `public`, `exportedToNamespace`), plus `HostnameAndNamespace` lookup map and precomputed `instancesByPort` |\n| `virtualServiceIndex` | VirtualServices bucketed by gateway, namespace, and `exportTo` scope |\n| `destinationRuleIndex` | `ConsolidatedDestRule` maps for namespace-local and namespace-exported DRs, with wildcard and exact-hostname separation |\n| `sidecarIndex` | `SidecarScope` objects per namespace \u2014 either user-defined or lazily generated defaults |\n| `gatewayIndex` | All `Gateway` resources by namespace |\n| `envoyFiltersByNamespace` | `EnvoyFilterWrapper` chains keyed by namespace |\n| `wasmPluginsByNamespace` | `WasmPluginWrapper` maps |\n| `AuthnPolicies` | `PeerAuthentication` and `RequestAuthentication` |\n| `AuthzPolicies` | `AuthorizationPolicy` resources |\n| `Telemetry` | `Telemetry` API resources |\n| `networkMgr` | Cross-network gateway topology |\n\nThe `ProxyStatus` map is writable during a push (protected by `proxyStatusMutex`); it accumulates per-proxy error events \u2014 such as conflicting listeners or clusters without instances \u2014 that are later published to Prometheus via `UpdateMetrics()`.\n\n### InitContext: Rebuilding the Snapshot\n\n`InitContext` (`push_context.go:~1340`) is the entry point called by `DiscoveryServer.initPushContext`. It uses a mutex to ensure only one goroutine builds a given version:\n\n- **Full rebuild** (`createNewContext`): Called when there is no prior `PushContext`, the push is `Forced`, or `pushReq == nil`. Calls all `initX` functions in dependency order:\n  1. `initServiceRegistry` \u2014 enumerates `env.Services()` (from the aggregate controller) and populates the service index\n  2. `initVirtualServices`, `initDestinationRules`, `initGateways`, `initEnvoyFilters`, etc.\n  3. `initSidecarScopes` \u2014 **must be last** because `SidecarScope` objects reference the virtual service and destination rule indexes\n\n- **Incremental update** (`updateContext`): Called when `pushReq.ConfigsUpdated` is non-nil and the push is not forced. The method inspects each changed `kind.Kind` and re-initializes only the affected sub-index, copying the old value for everything else. For example, a `DestinationRule` change re-runs `initDestinationRules` and `initSidecarScopes` but reuses `virtualServiceIndex`, `AuthnPolicies`, etc. unchanged.\n\nThis incremental path is the primary scalability mechanism: a gateway `Gateway` resource change does not recompute Telemetry, AuthZ, or VirtualService indexes.\n\n### Config Translation: VirtualService \u2192 RouteConfiguration\n\nPilot does not directly emit Envoy config in `PushContext`. The translation happens in the generator layer (`pilot/pkg/networking/core/`), which queries `PushContext` APIs during each push:\n\n- **CDS** (`pilot/pkg/networking/core/cluster.go`): `BuildClusters` calls `proxy.SidecarScope.Services()` to get the list of services visible to this proxy, then builds one or more `envoy.Cluster` protos per service port. For a service with a matching `DestinationRule`, cluster-level TLS settings, circuit breakers, and outlier detection are read from `PushContext.destinationRule(proxyNamespace, svc)`. For delta CDS (`BuildDeltaClusters`), only clusters for services in `ConfigsUpdated` are recomputed.\n\n- **EDS** (`pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`): `EdsGenerator.Generate` reads from `EndpointIndex` (the live shard table maintained by service registry controllers) and emits `ClusterLoadAssignment` protos. No `PushContext` rebuild is needed for EDS incremental pushes.\n\n- **LDS/RDS** (`pilot/pkg/networking/core/listener.go`, `route/route.go`): Listener chains and route configs are constructed by querying `PushContext.VirtualServicesForGateway` or traversing the `SidecarScope`'s egress listener list. Each `VirtualService` http/tcp/tls route block is translated into Envoy `Route`, `WeightedCluster`, retry policy, fault injection, and CORS filter config.\n\n- **SDS** (`pilot/pkg/xds/sds.go`): TLS certificate references are resolved against the credentials store.\n\nThe `findGenerator` method (`xdsgen.go:72`) resolves which generator to use in a three-step lookup: `proxy.Metadata.Generator + \"/\" + typeURL`, then `proxy.Type + \"/\" + typeURL`, then `typeURL` alone. This allows specialized generators for ztunnel (Workload/Address types) and gRPC proxyless clients without changing the common path.\n\n### Push Triggers and PushContext Regeneration\n\n| Trigger | Full PushContext rebuild? | EDS incremental? |\n|---|---|---|\n| Istio CRD change (VirtualService, DR, etc.) | Yes (via `ConfigUpdate` with `Full: true`) | No |\n| K8s Service added/deleted | Yes (via `SvcUpdate` \u2192 `ConfigUpdate` with `Full: true`) | No |\n| Pod endpoint change (scale-up / scale-down) | No | Yes (via `EDSUpdate`) |\n| JWT public key rotation | Yes (forced via `JwksResolver.PushFunc`) | No |\n| Debug trigger | No (uses existing `PushContext`) | No |\n\nA `PushRequest.Full = false` (EDS incremental) skips `initPushContext` entirely; the existing `PushContext` is reused, and only the `EndpointIndex` shards are updated.\n\n### Metrics and Error Tracking\n\n`PushContext.AddMetric(metric, key, proxyID, msg)` is called throughout the generator layer to record per-proxy anomalies:\n\n- `ProxyStatusConflictOutboundListenerTCPOverTCP` \u2014 two services on the same outbound port\n- `ProxyStatusConflictInboundListener` \u2014 two services selecting the same pod port\n- `EndpointNoPod` \u2014 an endpoint has no backing pod, so labels cannot be determined\n- `DuplicatedClusters` \u2014 two `ServiceEntry` resources share a hostname\n- `ProxyStatusClusterNoInstances` \u2014 a cluster has no healthy endpoints\n\nThese are accumulated in `ProxyStatus` (map of metric name \u2192 map of config key \u2192 `ProxyPushStatus`) and flushed to Prometheus via `UpdateMetrics()` on the 10s periodic tick or at the start of the next push.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go`, `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/multicluster.go`, `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\n### The ServiceRegistry Interface\n\n`model.XDSUpdater` (`push_context.go:327`) is the interface that every registry implementation calls back into the `DiscoveryServer`:\n\n```go\ntype XDSUpdater interface {\n    EDSUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, entry []*IstioEndpoint)\n    EDSCacheUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, entry []*IstioEndpoint)\n    SvcUpdate(shard ShardKey, hostname string, namespace string, event Event)\n    ConfigUpdate(req *PushRequest)\n    ProxyUpdate(clusterID cluster.ID, ip string)\n    RemoveShard(shardKey ShardKey)\n}\n```\n\n`DiscoveryServer` directly implements this interface. Registries call `EDSUpdate` when a pod's readiness changes; they call `SvcUpdate` when a Kubernetes `Service` is added, modified, or deleted; they call `ConfigUpdate` for everything that requires a full push.\n\n### The Kubernetes Controller\n\n`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go` wraps the Kubernetes informer framework. It maintains informers for:\n\n- `Service` objects \u2192 `SvcUpdate` on add/update/delete\n- `EndpointSlice` objects \u2192 `EDSUpdate` when endpoint addresses change\n- `Pod` objects \u2192 labels are cached for endpoint enrichment, and `ProxyUpdate` is triggered when a pod's labels change in a way that affects which services it's an endpoint of\n\nThe controller populates `EndpointIndex` shards identified by a `ShardKey` (a `{Provider, ClusterID}` tuple). Each shard stores the list of `IstioEndpoint` objects for that cluster's view of the service.\n\n### The Aggregate Controller\n\n`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go` implements `model.ServiceDiscovery` by multiplexing across all registered `serviceregistry.Instance` objects. Its `Services()` method (`aggregate/controller.go:309`) iterates all registries and merges services that appear in multiple Kubernetes clusters by hostname: the first occurrence creates the `Service`, and subsequent occurrences add entries to `Service.ClusterVIPs` via `mergeService()`. Non-Kubernetes registries (e.g., `ServiceEntry` via `serviceentry.Controller`) are included verbatim without deduplication.\n\nThe aggregate controller is also the fanout point for event handlers: when a registry calls `NotifyServiceHandlers`, the aggregate propagates to both the global handler list and any per-cluster handler lists registered by `RegisterHandlersForCluster`.\n\n### Multi-Cluster Support\n\n`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/multicluster.go` manages the lifecycle of one `kubeController` per remote cluster. The `Multicluster` struct uses `multicluster.BuildMultiClusterComponent` to watch the `istio-remote-secret` Secret for remote cluster kubeconfigs. When a new cluster secret is discovered:\n\n1. A new Kubernetes client is created for the remote cluster.\n2. A `kubeController` (wrapping a `kube/controller.Controller`) is instantiated for that cluster and registered with the aggregate controller via `AddRegistryAndRun`.\n3. The remote controller starts its informers, which will call `EDSUpdate` / `SvcUpdate` / `ConfigUpdate` on the shared `XDSUpdater` as it discovers services.\n\nWhen a remote cluster is removed (secret deleted), `kubeController.Close()` removes the registry from the aggregate, deletes its endpoint shards, and triggers a full push via `ConfigUpdate(Full: true, Reason: ClusterUpdate)`.\n\nEach remote cluster's controller uses the same `ShardKey`-based `EndpointIndex`. For a service that exists in both the local and a remote cluster, the `EndpointIndex` holds two shards: one from the local `{Kubernetes, local-cluster}` and one from `{Kubernetes, remote-cluster}`. The EDS generator merges both shards into a single `ClusterLoadAssignment`, applying locality-aware load balancing weights based on the proxy's cluster and network topology from `networkMgr`.\n\n### Endpoint Updates: EDS vs. Full Push\n\n`EDSUpdate` (`eds.go:47`) is the hot path for pod health changes:\n\n1. It calls `EndpointIndex.UpdateServiceEndpoints` which updates the named shard and returns a `pushType` (`IncrementalPush`, `FullPush`, or no push).\n2. `FullPush` is returned when the service's port mapping has changed (a new port was added), requiring a CDS rebuild. This triggers `ConfigUpdate(Full: true)`.\n3. `IncrementalPush` is returned for normal endpoint churn (pod added/removed/readiness flipped). This triggers `ConfigUpdate(Full: false)`.\n\n`EDSCacheUpdate` (`eds.go:70`) takes the same shard path but does **not** enqueue a push; it is used during bulk reconciliation (e.g., on registry startup) so that all shards are populated before the first push.\n\n### When Does a Service Change Trigger CDS vs. EDS?\n\n| Event | CDS Needed | EDS Needed |\n|---|---|---|\n| New service or service port added | Yes (new cluster name) | Yes (new endpoint group) |\n| Service port removed | Yes (cluster must be removed) | Implicitly (cluster gone) |\n| Pod endpoint added/removed | No | Yes |\n| Pod labels changed (affects service selection) | No | Yes (shard membership changes) |\n| `DestinationRule` subset added | Yes (new subset cluster) | No |\n| Service deleted | Yes (cluster removed) | Yes (shard cleared) |\n\nThe split is enforced in `eds.go:edsNeedsPush`: `skippedEdsConfigs` contains all config kinds (Gateway, VirtualService, WasmPlugin, etc.) that cannot affect endpoint membership, so EDS pushes skip config changes of those types without even consulting the generator.\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow: Config Change to Envoy Push\n\nThe following describes the complete path from an Istio CRD change to a proxy receiving updated xDS:\n\n```\n1. User applies VirtualService YAML\n2. Kubernetes API server stores it\n3. Istio CRD informer (crdclient) fires an Add/Update event\n4. ConfigController calls XDSUpdater.ConfigUpdate({Full: true, ConfigsUpdated: {VirtualService/name/ns}})\n5. DiscoveryServer.ConfigUpdate() increments InboundUpdates, appends to pushChannel\n6. debounce() accumulates events for DebounceAfter; merges concurrent changes\n7. DiscoveryServer.Push(req) is called:\n   a. oldPushContext.OnConfigChange() \u2192 saves metrics, resets Prometheus gauges\n   b. initPushContext() calls PushContext.InitContext()\n      - updateContext() detects VirtualService change \u2192 reinitializes virtualServiceIndex, sidecarIndex\n      - All other indexes copied from old PushContext\n   c. dropCacheForRequest() evicts cache entries depending on the changed VS\n   d. Env.SetPushContext(push) makes the new context globally visible\n8. AdsPushAll(req) \u2192 StartPush(req)\n9. For each Connection in adsClients: pushQueue.Enqueue(con, req)\n10. sendPushes() drains pushQueue with concurrentPushLimit semaphore\n11. For each dequeued (con, push):\n    a. Event{pushRequest} is sent to con.PushCh()\n    b. Connection.Push() calls pushConnection()\n12. pushConnection():\n    a. computeProxyState() updates SidecarScope for this proxy under the new PushContext\n    b. ProxyNeedsPush() filters ConfigsUpdated to configs this proxy depends on;\n       if empty, skip\n    c. For each watched resource type in PushOrder:\n       pushXds(con, watchedResource, req)\n13. pushXds():\n    a. findGenerator(typeURL, con) \u2192 e.g., CDS generator\n    b. gen.Generate(proxy, watchedResource, req)\n       - Reads SidecarScope.Services() from new PushContext\n       - Reads DestinationRules, EnvoyFilters from new PushContext\n       - Checks LRU cache; returns cached result or builds new resources\n    c. Wraps result in DiscoveryResponse with PushVersion nonce\n    d. xds.Send(con, resp) writes to the gRPC stream\n14. Envoy processes the response and ACKs\n15. processRequest() receives ACK (shouldRespond=false), no further work\n```\n\n---\n\n## Extension Points\n\n### Custom Generators\n\nThe `Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator` field is the primary extension surface. Any component that can access `DiscoveryServer` can register a generator:\n\n```go\ns.Generators[\"my-type-url\"] = myGenerator\ns.Generators[\"router/my-type-url\"] = gatewayOnlyGenerator\n```\n\nThe lookup in `findGenerator` (`xdsgen.go:72`) tries `metadata.Generator + \"/\" + typeURL`, then `proxyType + \"/\" + typeURL`, then bare `typeURL`. This allows registering type-specific generators for standard xDS types, or proxy-type-specific generators (e.g., ztunnel gets a different generator for `Address` and `WorkloadAuthorization` types). The `model.XdsResourceGenerator` and `model.XdsDeltaResourceGenerator` interfaces define `Generate` and `GenerateDeltas` methods respectively.\n\n### EnvoyFilter API\n\n`EnvoyFilter` resources in `envoyFiltersByNamespace` are applied in `pilot/pkg/networking/core/envoyfilter/` as post-processing patches on top of generated Envoy config. The patch model supports `MERGE`, `INSERT_BEFORE`, `INSERT_AFTER`, `REPLACE`, and `REMOVE` operations on listener filter chains, cluster fields, and route config. This is the main mechanism for users to inject custom Envoy configuration without forking Pilot.\n\n### WasmPlugin API\n\n`WasmPlugin` resources are translated into Envoy `ExtensionConfigDiscovery` (ECDS) resources by the ECDS generator (`pilot/pkg/xds/ecds.go`). Rather than inlining Wasm byte code in the listener config, the ECDS generator serves plugin URLs and runtime configuration over a separate xDS stream, allowing plugin updates without full LDS pushes.\n\n### Telemetry API\n\n`Telemetry` resources in `PushContext.Telemetry` control access log providers, metrics, and tracing configuration. The telemetry subsystem in `pilot/pkg/model/telemetry.go` translates `Telemetry` CRs into Envoy `HttpConnectionManager` filter configuration and stat prefixes. Users can reference extension providers defined in `MeshConfig.ExtensionProviders` to plug in arbitrary telemetry backends.\n\n### ProxyNeedsPush Hook\n\n`DiscoveryServer.ProxyNeedsPush` is a settable function (`discovery.go:78`). The default implementation calls `filterRelevantUpdates`. Replacing this function allows injecting custom skip logic \u2014 for example, in tests or specialized deployments where certain proxies should always or never receive a push.\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Connection Establishment Errors\n\n`initConnection` returns errors for:\n- Invalid `Node.Metadata` (returned as gRPC `InvalidArgument`)\n- Authorization failures from `authorize()` (returned as `PermissionDenied`)\n- Ztunnel connecting when ambient mode is disabled\n\nThese errors close the gRPC stream immediately. The client (Envoy) will retry with exponential backoff.\n\n### Push Failures\n\n`pushXds` checks the return from `xds.Send()`. If the send fails (e.g., gRPC write timeout, buffer full), it calls `recordSendError()` which increments a per-typeURL metric and logs a warning. The error propagates up through `pushConnection` \u2192 `Connection.Push`, and the goroutine in `doSendPushes` returns the error. The underlying gRPC stream is torn down, and `closeConnection()` removes the proxy from `adsClients`. The proxy will reconnect and receive a fresh full push.\n\nA push error for one proxy does not affect other proxies: the `pushQueue` worker is per-proxy goroutine, and errors are isolated.\n\n### Generator Errors\n\n`gen.Generate()` can return an error or `nil` resources. Both result in the push for that typeURL being skipped (the `if err != nil || res == nil` guard in `xdsgen.go:133`). Errors are logged but do not abort the push loop; the goroutine continues pushing other resource types. The proxy's watched resource is not updated, so Pilot will retry on the next push cycle.\n\n### PushContext Initialization Errors\n\n`InitContext` is not expected to fail in production \u2014 it reads from in-memory caches populated by informers. If a sub-initializer encounters a bad config object (e.g., an `EnvoyFilter` with invalid JSON), the error is recorded via `AddMetric` rather than panicking. The bad config is skipped and its absence is visible in the debug endpoint at `/debug/push_status`.\n\n### Config Validation\n\nIstio validates CRDs at admission time via the `validation` webhook (`pilot/pkg/config/kube/crd/config.go`). Objects that fail validation are rejected before reaching the informer. Objects that pass validation but produce runtime errors (e.g., a `DestinationRule` referencing a non-existent subset) are handled gracefully in the generator layer, which logs a warning and skips the invalid config.\n\n### Proxy Disconnects\n\n`closeConnection()` (`ads.go:283`) is called when a proxy's stream terminates. It:\n1. Removes the connection from `adsClients`.\n2. Calls `WorkloadEntryController.OnDisconnect(con)` so that auto-registered `WorkloadEntry` objects are drained.\n3. Records the disconnect in per-version Istio-version metrics.\n\nAny pending entry in `pushQueue` for that connection is handled by `doSendPushes` detecting that the stream context is done (via the `case <-closed` branch) and calling `doneFunc()` to release the semaphore without sending.\n\n---\n\n## Key Source Files Reference\n\n| File | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go` | `DiscoveryServer` struct, `NewDiscoveryServer`, debounce loop, `Push`, `StartPush` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go` | `Connection` type, `Stream`, `initConnection`, `processRequest`, `pushConnection`, `AdsPushAll` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/delta.go` | Delta (incremental) xDS stream handler `StreamDeltas` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/xdsgen.go` | `findGenerator`, `pushXds`, `xdsNeedsPush` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/pushqueue.go` | `PushQueue` \u2014 per-proxy coalescing queue with `Enqueue`/`Dequeue`/`MarkDone` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go` | `EDSUpdate`, `EDSCacheUpdate`, `EdsGenerator.Generate` |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/proxy_dependencies.go` | `filterRelevantUpdates`, `proxyDependentOnConfig` |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` | `PushContext`, all `initX` methods, `XDSUpdater` interface, `PushRequest`, `TriggerReason` |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/typed_xds_cache.go` | LRU xDS resource cache with config-dependent eviction |\n| `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go` | `EndpointIndex`, shard management |\n| `pilot/pkg/networking/core/cluster.go` | `BuildClusters`, `BuildDeltaClusters` \u2014 CDS generator |\n| `pilot/pkg/networking/core/listener.go` | LDS generator |\n| `pilot/pkg/networking/core/route/route.go` | RDS / `RouteConfiguration` builder |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/controller.go` | Multi-registry aggregation, `Services()` merge logic |\n| informer controller for Services, EndpointSlices, Pods |\n| `pilot/pkg/networking/core/envoyfilter/` | `EnvoyFilter` patch application to generated Envoy config |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/monitoring.go` | All push-related Prometheus metrics |\n",

# Istio Pilot Discovery Service: Architecture Document

## Overview

Istio Pilot's Discovery Service is the subsystem inside `istiod` that translates Istio's high-level mesh configuration into Envoy-specific xDS resources and streams those resources to every connected sidecar, gateway, and ztunnel proxy. The subsystem is built around four tightly coupled layers:

1. **`DiscoveryServer`** — the gRPC server that owns proxy connections and orchestrates pushes
2. **The ADS/Delta Connection Model** — the per-proxy streaming logic and push pipeline
3. **`PushContext`** — the immutable configuration snapshot computed before each fleet-wide push
4. **Service Registry** — the data source that tracks live services and endpoints

---

## 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server

**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`

### What It Owns

`DiscoveryServer` is the central coordinator. It implements the Envoy `AggregatedDiscoveryService` gRPC service and sits at the boundary between Istio's internal data model and Envoy's wire protocol. Its fields define every aspect of the push lifecycle:

| Field | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `adsClients map[string]*Connection` | Registry of every live proxy connection, keyed by connection ID |
| `pushChannel chan *model.PushRequest` | Inbound buffer for raw update events before debouncing |
| `pushQueue *PushQueue` | Ordered queue of (connection, pushRequest) pairs after debouncing |
| `concurrentPushLimit chan struct{}` | Semaphore limiting how many proxy pushes run in parallel (`features.PushThrottle`) |
| `RequestRateLimit *rate.Limiter` | Token-bucket rate limiter applied to new connection requests |
| `Cache model.XdsCache` | Shared LRU cache of already-generated xDS resources |
| `Generators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator` | Plugin map from
... (truncated)
